286→static PyObject *\n   287→array_inplace_matrix_multiply(PyArrayObject *self, PyObject *other)\n   288→{\n   289→    INPLACE_GIVE_UP_IF_NEEDED(self, other,\n   290→            nb_inplace_matrix_multiply, array_inplace_matrix_multiply);\n   291→\n   292→    PyObject *args = PyTuple_Pack(3, self, other, self);\n   293→    if (args == NULL) {\n   294→        return NULL;\n   295→    }\n   296→    PyObject *kwargs;\n   297→\n   298→    /*\n   299→     * Unlike `matmul(a, b, out=a)` we ensure that the result is not broadcast\n   300→     * if the result without `out` would have less dimensions than `a`.\n   301→     * Since the signature of matmul is '(n?,k),(k,m?)->(n?,m?)' this is the\n   302→     * case exactly when the second operand has both core dimensions.\n   303→     *\n   304→     * The error here will be confusing, but for now, we enforce this by\n   305→     * passing the correct `axes=`.\n   306→     */\n   307→    if (PyArray_NDIM(self) == 1) {\n   308→        kwargs = npy_static_pydata.axes_1d_obj_kwargs;\n   309→    }\n   310→    else {\n   311→        kwargs = npy_static_pydata.axes_2d_obj_kwargs;\n   312→    }\n   313→    PyObject *res = PyObject_Call(n_ops.matmul, args, kwargs);\n   314→    Py_DECREF(args);\n   315→\n   316→    if (res == NULL) {\n   317→        /*\n   318→         * AxisError should indicate that the axes argument didn't work out\n   319→         * which should mean the second operand not being 2 dimensional.\n   320→         */\n   321→        if (PyErr_ExceptionMatches(npy_static_pydata.AxisError)) {\n   322→            PyErr_SetString(PyExc_ValueError,\n   323→                \"inplace matrix multiplication requires the first operand to \"\n   324→                \"have at least one and the second at least two dimensions.\");\n   325→        }\n   326→    }\n   327→\n   328→    return res;\n   329→}\n   330→\n   331→static int\n   332→fast_scalar_power(PyObject *o1, PyObject *o2, int inplace, PyObject **result)\n   333→{\n   334→    PyObject *fastop = NULL;\n   335→\n   336→    if (PyLong_CheckExact(o2)) {\n   337→        int overflow = 0;\n   338→        long exp = PyLong_AsLongAndOverflow(o2, &overflow);\n   339→        if (overflow != 0) {\n   340→            return -1;\n   341→        }\n   342→\n   343→        if (exp == -1) {\n   344→            fastop = n_ops.reciprocal;\n   345→        }\n   346→        else if (exp == 2) {\n   347→            fastop = n_ops.square;\n   348→        }\n   349→        else {\n   350→            return 1;\n   351→        }\n   352→    }\n   353→    else if (PyFloat_CheckExact(o2)) {\n   354→        double exp = PyFloat_AsDouble(o2);\n   355→        if (exp == 0.5) {\n   356→            fastop = n_ops.sqrt;\n   357→        }\n   358→        else {\n   359→            return 1;\n   360→        }\n   361→    }\n   362→    else {\n   363→        return 1;\n   364→    }\n   365→\n   366→    PyArrayObject *a1 = (PyArrayObject *)o1;\n   367→    if (PyArray_ISOBJECT(a1)) {\n   368→        return 1;\n   369→    }\n   370→    if (fastop != n_ops.square && !PyArray_ISFLOAT(a1) && !PyArray_ISCOMPLEX(a1)) {\n   371→        // we special-case squaring for any array type\n   372→        // gh-29388\n   373→        return 1;\n   374→    }\n   375→\n   376→    if (inplace || can_elide_temp_unary(a1)) {\n   377→        *result = PyArray_GenericInplaceUnaryFunction(a1, fastop);\n   378→    }\n   379→    else {\n   380→        *result = PyArray_GenericUnaryFunction(a1, fastop);\n   381→    }\n   382→\n   383→    return 0;\n   384→}\n   385→\n   386→static PyObject *\n   387→array_power(PyObject *a1, PyObject *o2, PyObject *modulo)\n   388→{\n   389→    PyObject *value = NULL;\n   390→\n   391→    if (modulo != Py_None) {\n   392→        /* modular exponentiation is not implemented (gh-8804) */\n   393→        Py_INCREF(Py_NotImplemented);\n   394→        return Py_NotImplemented;\n   395→    }\n   396→\n   397→    BINOP_GIVE_UP_IF_NEEDED(a1, o2, nb_power, array_power);\n   398→    if (fast_scalar_power(a1, o2, 0, &value) != 0) {\n   399→        value = PyArray_GenericBinaryFunction(a1, o2, n_ops.power);\n   400→    }\n   401→    return value;\n   402→}\n   403→\n   404→static PyObject *\n   405→array_positive(PyArrayObject *m1)\n   406→{\n   407→    if (can_elide_temp_unary(m1)) {\n                           n_ops.true_divide);\n   630→}\n   631→\n   632→\n   633→static int\n   634→_array_nonzero(PyArrayObject *mp)\n   635→{\n   636→    npy_intp n;\n   637→\n   638→    n = PyArray_SIZE(mp);\n   639→    if (n == 1) {\n   640→        int res;\n   641→        if (Py_EnterRecursiveCall(\" while converting array to bool\")) {\n   642→            return -1;\n   643→        }\n   644→        res = PyDataType_GetArrFuncs(PyArray_DESCR(mp))->nonzero(PyArray_DATA(mp), mp);\n   645→        /* nonzero has no way to indicate an error, but one can occur */\n   646→        if (PyErr_Occurred()) {\n   647→            res = -1;\n   648→        }\n   649→        Py_LeaveRecursiveCall();\n   650→        return res;\n   651→    }\n   652→    else if (n == 0) {\n   653→        PyErr_SetString(PyExc_ValueError,\n   654→                \"The truth value of an empty array is ambiguous. \"\n   655→                \"Use `array.size > 0` to check that an array is not empty.\");\n   656→        return -1;\n   657→    }\n   658→    else {\n   659→        PyErr_SetString(PyExc_ValueError,\n   660→                        \"The truth value of an array \"\n   661→                        \"with more than one element is ambiguous. \"\n   662→                        \"Use a.any() or a.all()\");\n   663→        return -1;\n   664→    }\n   665→}\n   666→\n   667→/*\n   668→ * Convert the array to a scalar if allowed, and apply the builtin function\n   669→ * to it. The where argument is passed onto Py_EnterRecursiveCall when the\n   670→ * array contains python objects.\n   671→ */\n   672→NPY_NO_EXPORT PyObject *\n   673→array_scalar_forward(PyArrayObject *v,\n   674→                     PyObject *(*builtin_func)(PyObject *),\n   675→                     const char *where)\n   676→{\n   677→    if (check_is_convertible_to_scalar(v) < 0) {\n   678→        return NULL;\n   679→    }\n   680→\n   681→    PyObject *scalar;\n   682→    scalar = PyArray_GETITEM(v, PyArray_DATA(v));\n   683→    if (scalar == NULL) {\n   684→        return NULL;\n   685→    }\n   686→\n   687→    /* Need to guard against recursion if our array holds references */\n   688→    if (PyDataType_REFCHK(PyArray_DESCR(v))) {\n   689→        PyObject *res;\n   690→        if (Py_EnterRecursiveCall(where) != 0) {\n   691→            Py_DECREF(scalar);\n   692→            return NULL;\n   693→        }\n   694→        res = builtin_func(scalar);\n   695→        Py_DECREF(scalar);\n   696→        Py_LeaveRecursiveCall();\n   697→        return res;\n   698→    }\n   699→    else {\n   700→        PyObject *res;\n   701→        res = builtin_func(scalar);\n   702→        Py_DECREF(scalar);\n   703→        return res;\n   704→    }\n   705→}\n   706→\n   707→\n   708→NPY_NO_EXPORT PyObject *\n   709→array_float(PyArrayObject *v)\n   710→{\n   711→    return array_scalar_forward(v, &PyNumber_Float, \" in ndarray.__float__\");\n   712→}\n   713→\n   714→NPY_NO_EXPORT PyObject *\n   715→array_int(PyArrayObject *v)\n   716→{\n   717→    return array_scalar_forward(v, &PyNumber_Long, \" in ndarray.__int__\");\n   718→}\n   719→\n   720→static PyObject *\n   721→array_index(PyArrayObject *v)\n   722→{\n   723→    if (!PyArray_ISINTEGER(v) ||  }\n   728→    return PyArray_GETITEM(v, PyArray_DATA(v));\n   729→}\n   730→\n   731→\n   732→NPY_NO_EXPORT PyNumberMethods array_as_number = {\n   733→    .nb_add = array_add,\n   734→ PyDataType_GetArrFuncs(PyArray_DESCR(mp))->nonzero(PyArray_DATA(mp), mp);\n        /* nonzero has no way to indicate an error, but one can occur */\n        if (PyErr_Occurred()) {\n            res = The where argument is passed onto Py_EnterRecursiveCall when the\n * array contains python objects.\n */\nNPY_NO_EXPORT PyObject *\narray_scalar_forward(PyArrayObject *v,\n                     PyObject *(*builtin_func)(PyObject *),\n                     const char *where)\n{\n    if (check_is_convertible_to_scalar(v) < 0) {\n        return NULL;\n    }\n\n    PyObject *scalar;\n    scalar = PyArray_GETITEM(v, PyArray_DATA(v));\n    if (scalar == NULL) {\n        return NULL;\n    }\n\n    /* Need to guard against recursion if our array holds references */\n    if The default,\n        axis=None, will sum all of the elements of the input array.  If\n        axis is negative it counts from the last to the first axis. If\n        axis is a tuple of ints, a sum is performed on all of the axes\n        specified in the tuple instead of a single axis or all the axes as\n        before.\n    dtype : dtype, optional\n        The type of the returned array and of the accumulator in which the\n        elements are summed.  The dtype of `a` is used by default unless `a`\n        has an integer dtype of less precision than the default platform\n        integer.  In that case, if `a` is signed then the platform integer\n        is used while if `a` is unsigned then an unsigned integer of the\n        same precision as the platform integer is used.\n    out : ndarray, optional\n        Alternative output array in which to place the result. It must have\n        the same shape as the expected output, but the type of the output\n        values will be cast if necessary.\n    keepdims : bool, optional\n        If this is set to True, the axes which are reduced are left\n        in the result as dimensions with size one. With this option,\n        the result will broadcast correctly against the input array.\n\n        If the default value is passed, then `keepdims` will not be\n        passed through to the `sum` method of sub-classes of\n        `ndarray`, however any non-default value will be.  If the\n        sub-class' method does not implement `keepdims` any\n        exceptions will be raised.\n    initial : scalar, optional\n        Starting value for the sum. See `~numpy.ufunc.reduce` for details.\n    where : array_like of bool, optional\n        Elements to include in the sum. See `~numpy.ufunc.reduce` for details.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    sum_along_axis : ndarray\n        An array with the same shape as `a`, with the specified\n        axis removed.   If `a` is a 0-d array, or if `axis` is None, a scalar\n        is returned.  If an output array is specified, a reference to\n        `out` is returned.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    ndarray.sum : Equivalent method.\n    add: ``numpy.add.reduce`` equivalent function.\n    cumsum : Cumulative sum of array elements.\n    trapezoid : Integration of array values using composite trapezoidal rule.\n\n    mean, average\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    Arithmetic is modular when using integer types, and no error is\n    raised on overflow.\n\n    The sum of an empty array is the neutral element 0:\n\n    >>> np.sum([])\n    0.0\n\n    For floating point numbers the numerical precision of sum (and\n    ``np.add.reduce``) is in general limited by directly adding each number\n    individually to the result causing rounding errors in every step.\n    However, often numpy will use a  numerically better approach (partial\n    pairwise summation) leading to improved precision in many use-cases.\n    This improved precision is always provided when no ``axis`` is given.\n    When ``axis`` is given, it will depend on which axis is summed.\n    Technically, to provide the best speed possible, the improved precision\n    is only used when the summation is along the fast axis in memory.\n    Note that the exact precision may vary depending on other parameters.\n    In contrast to NumPy, Python's ``math.fsum`` function uses a slower but\n    more precise approach to summation.\n    Especially when summing a large number of lower precision floating point\n    numbers, such as ``float32``, numerical errors can become significant.\n    In such cases it can be Build einsum string for the reduction\n+    # Map each dimension to a letter\n+    index_letters = ''.join(chr(ord('a') + i) for i in range(min(ndim, 26)))\n+    if ndim > 26:\n+        # Fallback to umr_sum if too many dimensions\n+        return umr_sum(a, axis, dtype, None, keepdims)\n+\n+    input_str = index_letters[:ndim]\n+\n+    # Determine which axes to keep\n+    kept_axes = [i for i in range(ndim) if i not in axis_normalized]\n+\n+    # Build output string\n+    if keepdims:\n+        output_str = ''\n+        for i in range(ndim):\n+            if i not in axis_normalized:\n+                output_str += input_str[i]\n+    else:\n+        output_str = ''.join(input_str[i] for i in kept_axes)\n+\n+    einsum_str = f'{input_str}->{output_str}'\n+\n+    # Perform einsum with type conversion\n+    if out_dtype is None:\n+        result = einsum(einsum_str, a_work, optimize='greedy')\n+    else:\n+        result = einsum(einsum_str, a_work, optimize='greedy').astype(out_dtype, copy=False)\n+\n+    if keepdims:\n+        result_shape = [1 if i in axis_normalized else a.shape[i] for i in range(ndim)]\n+        result = result.reshape(result_shape)\n+\n+    return result\n","numLines":119,"startLine":1,"totalLines":119}}}
